## **1. System Architecture Overview**

We can divide the ecosystem into **four main modules**, with an optional **core database/service layer** to handle storage, retrieval, and tracking.

### **A. Textbooks & Class Notes**
- **Function:** Provides curated or AI-generated learning material.
- **Features:**
  - Modular content (chapters, sections, subsections)
  - Interactive elements (examples, exercises, images, diagrams)
  - Version control (track updates)
  - Exportable in PDF, HTML, or in-game readable formats

### **B. Homework & Assignments**
- **Function:** Auto-generate practice problems and project-based tasks.
- **Features:**
  - Configurable difficulty levels
  - Multiple question types: multiple choice, short answer, coding, essay
  - Time limits and due dates
  - Automated grading engine (for objective tasks)
  - Adaptive assignments based on student performance

### **C. Exams & Quizzes**
- **Function:** Procedurally generate assessments.
- **Features:**
  - Randomized question pools
  - Multiple formats (MCQ, short answer, essays)
  - Secure, timed tests
  - Detailed scoring with feedback

### **D. Research & Documentation**
- **Function:** Provide a digital notebook/knowledge base inside the game.
- **Features:**
  - Rich text editor with formatting
  - Tagging and linking between notes
  - Citation support
  - Versioning for iterative research
  - Searchable database of student work

### **E. Core Data/Service Layer**
- Handles:
  - User authentication and roles (student, teacher, admin)
  - Storage of notes, assignments, exams, and textbooks
  - Analytics (progress tracking, performance metrics)
  - Procedural generation algorithms
  - In-game integration (if needed)

---

## **2. Procedural Generation Logic**

We can define **templates** for each content type:

- **Textbook Chapter Template**
```json
{
  "title": "Chapter Title",
  "learning_objectives": ["Objective 1", "Objective 2"],
  "sections": [
    {
      "section_title": "Section 1",
      "content": "Text content with examples",
      "exercises": ["Exercise 1", "Exercise 2"]
    }
  ],
  "summary": "Chapter summary"
}
```

- **Assignment Template**
```json
{
  "title": "Assignment Title",
  "subject": "Math/Science/etc",
  "difficulty": "easy/medium/hard",
  "questions": [
    {
      "type": "multiple_choice",
      "prompt": "Question text",
      "options": ["A", "B", "C", "D"],
      "answer": "B"
    }
  ],
  "due_date": "YYYY-MM-DD",
  "auto_grade": true
}
```

- **Research Entry Template**
```json
{
  "title": "Note/Research Title",
  "tags": ["Physics", "Quantum Mechanics"],
  "content": "Full rich-text content with embedded links",
  "citations": ["Author, Year, Source"],
  "created_at": "timestamp",
  "updated_at": "timestamp"
}
```

### **5. Procedural Generator Stubs**

#### **textbook_generator.py**
```python
import json

def generate_chapter(title, objectives, sections, summary, filename):
    chapter = {
        "title": title,
        "learning_objectives": objectives,
        "sections": sections,
        "summary": summary
    }
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump(chapter, f, indent=4)
    print(f"Chapter saved to {filename}")

# Example usage
if __name__ == "__main__":
    sections = [
        {
            "section_title": "Sample Section",
            "content": "This is sample content.",
            "exercises": ["Exercise 1", "Exercise 2"]
        }
    ]
    generate_chapter("Sample Chapter", ["Objective 1"], sections, "Summary here", "../textbooks/sample_chapter.json")
```

#### **assignment_generator.py**
```python
import json

def generate_assignment(title, subject, difficulty, questions, due_date, filename):
    assignment = {
        "title": title,
        "subject": subject,
        "difficulty": difficulty,
        "questions": questions,
        "due_date": due_date,
        "auto_grade": True
    }
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump(assignment, f, indent=4)
    print(f"Assignment saved to {filename}")

# Example usage
if __name__ == "__main__":
    questions = [
        {
            "type": "multiple_choice",
            "prompt": "Sample Question?",
            "options": ["A", "B", "C", "D"],
            "answer": "A"
        }
    ]
    generate_assignment("Sample Assignment", "Math", "easy", questions, "2026-02-15", "../assignments/sample_assignment.json")
```

#### **exam_generator.py**
```python
import json

def generate_exam(title, subject, questions, time_limit, filename):
    exam = {
        "title": title,
        "subject": subject,
        "questions": questions,
        "time_limit_minutes": time_limit
    }
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump(exam, f, indent=4)
    print(f"Exam saved to {filename}")

# Example usage
if __name__ == "__main__":
    questions = [
        {"type": "short_answer", "prompt": "Sample Exam Question"}
    ]
    generate_exam("Sample Exam", "Math", questions, 60, "../exams/sample_exam.json")
```

## **1. Updated Procedural Generator Framework**

We'll enhance the stubs to support:

- **Dynamic chapter/section generation** (random examples, exercises)
- **Assignment question randomization** (difficulty levels, question pools)
- **Exam question pools with randomization** (to minimize duplication)
- **Per-student content** (using student IDs to seed randomness)

---

### **1A. Textbook Generator - Full Auto**

```python
import json
import random

def generate_chapter(student_id, subject, chapter_number):
    random.seed(student_id + chapter_number)  # Ensures unique content per student
    title = f"{subject} Chapter {chapter_number}: {random.choice(['Introduction', 'Basics', 'Fundamentals'])}"
    objectives = [
        f"Understand {random.choice(['variables', 'functions', 'equations'])}",
        f"Solve basic {random.choice(['problems', 'examples', 'questions'])}"
    ]
    sections = []
    for i in range(1, 3):
        section_title = f"Section {i}: {random.choice(['Concepts', 'Examples', 'Practice'])}"
        content = f"This section explains {random.choice(['variables', 'constants', 'algebraic operations'])}."
        exercises = [f"Solve {random.randint(1,10)}x + {random.randint(1,10)} = {random.randint(10,20)}" for _ in range(2)]
        sections.append({
            "section_title": section_title,
            "content": content,
            "exercises": exercises
        })
    summary = "This chapter covered basic concepts with examples and exercises."
    
    filename = f"textbooks/{subject.lower()}_chapter_{chapter_number}_student_{student_id}.json"
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump({
            "title": title,
            "learning_objectives": objectives,
            "sections": sections,
            "summary": summary
        }, f, indent=4)
    
    print(f"Textbook chapter saved: {filename}")
    return filename
```

---

### **1B. Assignment Generator - Full Auto**

```python
import json
import random

def generate_assignment(student_id, subject, assignment_number, difficulty='medium'):
    random.seed(student_id + assignment_number)
    
    title = f"{subject} Assignment {assignment_number}"
    questions = []
    num_questions = {'easy':3, 'medium':5, 'hard':7}[difficulty]
    
    for i in range(num_questions):
        a = random.randint(1,10)
        b = random.randint(1,10)
        q_type = random.choice(['multiple_choice', 'short_answer'])
        if q_type == 'multiple_choice':
            answer = a + b
            options = [answer, answer+1, answer-1, answer+2]
            random.shuffle(options)
            questions.append({
                "type":"multiple_choice",
                "prompt": f"Solve {a} + {b} = ?",
                "options": options,
                "answer": answer
            })
        else:
            questions.append({
                "type":"short_answer",
                "prompt": f"Solve {a} * {b} = ?"
            })
    
    filename = f"assignments/{subject.lower()}_assignment_{assignment_number}_student_{student_id}.json"
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump({
            "title": title,
            "subject": subject,
            "difficulty": difficulty,
            "questions": questions,
            "auto_grade": True
        }, f, indent=4)
    
    print(f"Assignment saved: {filename}")
    return filename
```

---

### **1C. Exam Generator - Full Auto**

```python
import json
import random

def generate_exam(student_id, subject, exam_number, time_limit=60):
    random.seed(student_id + exam_number)
    
    title = f"{subject} Exam {exam_number}"
    questions = []
    for i in range(5):
        a = random.randint(1,15)
        b = random.randint(1,15)
        q_type = random.choice(['multiple_choice', 'short_answer'])
        if q_type == 'multiple_choice':
            answer = a + b
            options = [answer, answer+1, answer-1, answer+2]
            random.shuffle(options)
            questions.append({
                "type":"multiple_choice",
                "prompt": f"Solve {a} + {b} = ?",
                "options": options,
                "answer": answer
            })
        else:
            questions.append({
                "type":"short_answer",
                "prompt": f"Solve {a} * {b} = ?"
            })
    
    filename = f"exams/{subject.lower()}_exam_{exam_number}_student_{student_id}.json"
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump({
            "title": title,
            "subject": subject,
            "questions": questions,
            "time_limit_minutes": time_limit
        }, f, indent=4)
    
    print(f"Exam saved: {filename}")
    return filename
```

### **2. Main App - Generate All Resources for a Student**

```python
from procedural_generators import textbook_generator, assignment_generator, exam_generator

def generate_resources_for_student(student_id, subject):
    print(f"Generating resources for Student {student_id}, Subject: {subject}")
    
    # Generate 3 chapters
    for chapter_number in range(1,4):
        textbook_generator.generate_chapter(student_id, subject, chapter_number)
    
    # Generate 2 assignments
    for assignment_number in range(1,3):
        assignment_generator.generate_assignment(student_id, subject, assignment_number, difficulty='medium')
    
    # Generate 1 exam
    exam_generator.generate_exam(student_id, subject, exam_number=1)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example: generate for student 101, subject Math
    generate_resources_for_student(101, "Math")
```

We'll implement this as a **per-student JSON-based notebook** with helper functions for creating, updating, and searching notes.  

---

### **1. Research Notebook Module - `research_notebook.py`**

```python
import json
import os
from datetime import datetime

RESEARCH_FOLDER = "research"

# Ensure the folder exists
os.makedirs(RESEARCH_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

def get_student_file(student_id):
    return f"{RESEARCH_FOLDER}/student_{student_id}_notes.json"

def load_notes(student_id):
    filename = get_student_file(student_id)
    if os.path.exists(filename):
        with open(filename, "r") as f:
            return json.load(f)
    return []

def save_notes(student_id, notes):
    filename = get_student_file(student_id)
    with open(filename, "w") as f:
        json.dump(notes, f, indent=4)
    print(f"Saved {len(notes)} notes for student {student_id}")

def add_note(student_id, title, content, tags=None, citations=None):
    tags = tags or []
    citations = citations or []
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    timestamp = datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
    
    note = {
        "title": title,
        "content": content,
        "tags": tags,
        "citations": citations,
        "created_at": timestamp,
        "updated_at": timestamp
    }
    notes.append(note)
    save_notes(student_id, notes)
    return note

def update_note(student_id, note_index, content=None, tags=None, citations=None):
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    if note_index < 0 or note_index >= len(notes):
        print("Invalid note index")
        return None
    
    note = notes[note_index]
    if content: note['content'] = content
    if tags: note['tags'] = tags
    if citations: note['citations'] = citations
    note['updated_at'] = datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
    
    notes[note_index] = note
    save_notes(student_id, notes)
    return note

def search_notes(student_id, query):
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    results = []
    for note in notes:
        if query.lower() in note['title'].lower() or query.lower() in note['content'].lower() or query.lower() in " ".join(note['tags']).lower():
            results.append(note)
    return results
```

---

### **2. Example Usage**

```python
from research_notebook import add_note, update_note, search_notes

STUDENT_ID = 101

# Add a new note
add_note(
    STUDENT_ID,
    title="Variables in Algebra",
    content="Variables represent unknown values. Example: x + 5 = 10",
    tags=["Algebra", "Variables"],
    citations=["MathTextbook, 2026"]
)

# Update the note
update_note(
    STUDENT_ID,
    note_index=0,
    content="Variables represent unknown values and can be manipulated in equations."
)

# Search notes
results = search_notes(STUDENT_ID, "variables")
print(f"Found {len(results)} notes:")
for note in results:
    print(f"- {note['title']}: {note['content']}")
```

### **3. Integration with Procedural Generation**

We can now **link notes to chapters, assignments, and exams** automatically:

- When a chapter is generated, the system can create an **empty research note** with the chapter title for the student.
- When an assignment or exam is generated, a note can be created for **problem-solving strategies** or **answer annotations**.

Example integration snippet in `main.py`:

```python
from research_notebook import add_note

def generate_chapter_with_note(student_id, subject, chapter_number):
    chapter_file = textbook_generator.generate_chapter(student_id, subject, chapter_number)
    chapter_title = f"{subject} Chapter {chapter_number}"
    add_note(student_id, title=chapter_title, content=f"Research notes for {chapter_title}")
    return chapter_file
```

Perfect! Let's build a **fully automated workflow** that generates **everything for a student in one run**:  

- **Textbooks** (per chapter)

---

### **1. Master Generator - `main.py`**

```python
from procedural_generators import textbook_generator, assignment_generator, exam_generator
from research_notebook import add_note
import os

def generate_student_resources(student_id, subject):
    print(f"Generating all resources for Student {student_id} - Subject: {subject}")
    
    # Ensure folders exist
    os.makedirs("textbooks", exist_ok=True)
    os.makedirs("assignments", exist_ok=True)
    os.makedirs("exams", exist_ok=True)
    os.makedirs("research", exist_ok=True)
    
    # --- 1. Generate Textbook Chapters and Linked Notes ---
    num_chapters = 3
    for chapter_number in range(1, num_chapters + 1):
        chapter_file = textbook_generator.generate_chapter(student_id, subject, chapter_number)
        chapter_title = f"{subject} Chapter {chapter_number}"
        add_note(
            student_id,
            title=f"Notes: {chapter_title}",
            content=f"Research notes for {chapter_title}",
            tags=[subject, "Chapter", f"Chapter {chapter_number}"]
        )
    
    # --- 2. Generate Assignments and Linked Notes ---
    num_assignments = 2
    for assignment_number in range(1, num_assignments + 1):
        assignment_file = assignment_generator.generate_assignment(student_id, subject, assignment_number, difficulty='medium')
        add_note(
            student_id,
            title=f"Strategy: Assignment {assignment_number}",
            content=f"Problem-solving strategies for Assignment {assignment_number}",
            tags=[subject, "Assignment", f"Assignment {assignment_number}"]
        )
    
    # --- 3. Generate Exam and Linked Notes ---
    exam_file = exam_generator.generate_exam(student_id, subject, exam_number=1, time_limit=60)
    add_note(
        student_id,
        title=f"Strategy: Exam 1",
        content="Preparation notes and key concepts for Exam 1",
        tags=[subject, "Exam"]
    )
    
    print(f"All resources generated for Student {student_id}!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example: generate resources for student 101 in Math
    generate_student_resources(student_id=101, subject="Math")
```

### **2. Helper Function: Export JSON to Text File**

```python
import os
import json

def export_json_to_txt(student_id, json_file, txt_filename, section_keys=None):
    """
    Convert a JSON resource to a readable text file for the student desktop.
    section_keys: list of keys to include in the text file (e.g., ['title', 'content'])
    """
    with open(json_file, "r") as f:
        data = json.load(f)
    
    content_lines = []
    
    if section_keys:
        for key in section_keys:
            if key in data:
                content_lines.append(f"{key.upper()}:\n{data[key]}\n")
    else:
        # default: dump everything as readable text
        def flatten_json(d, prefix=""):
            lines = []
            for k, v in d.items():
                if isinstance(v, dict):
                    lines += flatten_json(v, prefix=f"{prefix}{k}.")
                elif isinstance(v, list):
                    lines.append(f"{prefix}{k}:")
                    for item in v:
                        if isinstance(item, dict):
                            for subk, subv in item.items():
                                lines.append(f"  {subk}: {subv}")
                        else:
                            lines.append(f"  - {item}")
                else:
                    lines.append(f"{prefix}{k}: {v}")
            return lines
        content_lines = flatten_json(data)
    
    os.makedirs(f"student_desktops/student_{student_id}", exist_ok=True)
    txt_path = f"student_desktops/student_{student_id}/{txt_filename}"
    with open(txt_path, "w") as f:
        f.write("\n".join(content_lines))
    
    print(f"Exported {txt_path}")
    return txt_path
```

### **3. Integration with Master Generator**

We'll modify `generate_student_resources` to **export all JSON resources as text files** after generation:

```python
from procedural_generators import textbook_generator, assignment_generator, exam_generator
from research_notebook import add_note, load_notes
from export_helpers import export_json_to_txt

def generate_student_resources(student_id, subject):
    print(f"Generating all resources for Student {student_id} - Subject: {subject}")
    
    # --- 1. Textbooks ---
    textbook_files = []
    for chapter_number in range(1, 4):
        chapter_file = textbook_generator.generate_chapter(student_id, subject, chapter_number)
        chapter_title = f"{subject} Chapter {chapter_number}"
        add_note(student_id, title=f"Notes: {chapter_title}", content=f"Research notes for {chapter_title}", tags=[subject, "Chapter", f"Chapter {chapter_number}"])
        textbook_files.append((chapter_file, f"{subject}_Chapter_{chapter_number}.txt"))
    
    # --- 2. Assignments ---
    assignment_files = []
    for assignment_number in range(1, 3):
        assignment_file = assignment_generator.generate_assignment(student_id, subject, assignment_number, difficulty='medium')
        add_note(student_id, title=f"Strategy: Assignment {assignment_number}", content=f"Problem-solving strategies for Assignment {assignment_number}", tags=[subject, "Assignment", f"Assignment {assignment_number}"])
        assignment_files.append((assignment_file, f"Assignment_{assignment_number}.txt"))
    
    # --- 3. Exam ---
    exam_file = exam_generator.generate_exam(student_id, subject, exam_number=1, time_limit=60)
    add_note(student_id, title=f"Strategy: Exam 1", content="Preparation notes and key concepts for Exam 1", tags=[subject, "Exam"])
    
    # --- 4. Export Research Notes ---
    research_notes_file = f"student_desktops/student_{student_id}/Research_Notes.txt"
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    with open(research_notes_file, "w") as f:
        for note in notes:
            f.write(f"TITLE: {note['title']}\nTAGS: {', '.join(note['tags'])}\nCONTENT: {note['content']}\nCREATED: {note['created_at']}\nUPDATED: {note['updated_at']}\n\n")
    print(f"Exported {research_notes_file}")
    
    # --- 5. Export JSON resources as text files ---
    for json_file, txt_file in textbook_files + assignment_files + [(exam_file, "Exam_1.txt")]:
        export_json_to_txt(student_id, json_file, txt_file)
    
    print(f"All resources generated and exported to simulated desktop for Student {student_id}")
```

2. Each student gets a **"desktop folder"** with `.txt` files ready to read.  
3. Notes are **linked to chapters, assignments, and exams** for easy reference.

### **1. Simulated Desktop Module - `desktop_simulator.py`**

```python
import os

DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"

def list_files(student_id):
    folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
    if not os.path.exists(folder):
        print("No desktop found for this student.")
        return []
    
    files = os.listdir(folder)
    files = [f for f in files if f.endswith(".txt")]
    
    if not files:
        print("No text files found on the desktop.")
    else:
        print(f"Files on Student {student_id}'s desktop:")
        for i, file in enumerate(files):
            print(f"{i + 1}. {file}")
    return files

def open_file(student_id, file_index):
    folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
    files = [f for f in os.listdir(folder) if f.endswith(".txt")]
    
    if file_index < 1 or file_index > len(files):
        print("Invalid file index")
        return
    
    file_to_open = os.path.join(folder, files[file_index - 1])
    print(f"\n--- Opening {files[file_index - 1]} ---\n")
    with open(file_to_open, "r") as f:
        print(f.read())
    print("\n--- End of File ---\n")
```

```python
if files:
    open_file(STUDENT_ID, 1)  # Open the first file
```

3. `open_file(student_id, file_index)` opens the file in the terminal and displays content.  

✅ **This creates a realistic "desktop" feel** while remaining fully functional in a text-based environment.

### **1. Enhanced Desktop Simulator - `interactive_desktop.py`**

```python
import os

DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"

# Define default folders for organization
DEFAULT_FOLDERS = ["Chapters", "Assignments", "Exams", "Research"]

def setup_desktop(student_id):
    """Ensure desktop folders exist."""
    student_folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
    os.makedirs(student_folder, exist_ok=True)
    for folder in DEFAULT_FOLDERS:
        os.makedirs(os.path.join(student_folder, folder), exist_ok=True)
    return student_folder

def list_files(student_folder, folder_name=None):
    """List files in the desktop or a subfolder."""
    folder = student_folder if not folder_name else os.path.join(student_folder, folder_name)
    files = [f for f in os.listdir(folder) if f.endswith(".txt")]
    if not files:
        print("No files found here.")
        return []
    for i, file in enumerate(files):
        print(f"{i + 1}. {file}")
    return files

def open_file(student_folder, folder_name, file_index):
    folder = student_folder if not folder_name else os.path.join(student_folder, folder_name)
    files = [f for f in os.listdir(folder) if f.endswith(".txt")]
    if file_index < 1 or file_index > len(files):
        print("Invalid file number.")
        return
    file_to_open = os.path.join(folder, files[file_index - 1])
    print(f"\n--- Opening {files[file_index - 1]} ---\n")
    with open(file_to_open, "r") as f:
        print(f.read())
    print("\n--- End of File ---\n")

def search_files(student_folder, query):
    """Search all text files for a query string."""
    matches = []
    for root, _, files in os.walk(student_folder):
        for file in files:
            if file.endswith(".txt"):
                path = os.path.join(root, file)
                with open(path, "r") as f:
                    if query.lower() in f.read().lower():
                        matches.append(os.path.relpath(path, student_folder))
    if matches:
        print(f"Found {len(matches)} matching files:")
        for i, match in enumerate(matches):
            print(f"{i + 1}. {match}")
    else:
        print("No matches found.")
    return matches

def interactive_desktop(student_id):
    student_folder = setup_desktop(student_id)
    
    while True:
        print("\n=== Student Desktop ===")
        print("Folders: ", ", ".join(DEFAULT_FOLDERS))
        print("Options: [open folder] [search] [exit]")
        choice = input("Enter command: ").strip().lower()
        
        if choice == "exit":
            print("Exiting desktop.")
            break
        elif choice.startswith("open"):
            parts = choice.split()
            if len(parts) < 2:
                print("Specify folder to open: Chapters, Assignments, Exams, Research")
                continue
            folder_name = parts[1].capitalize()
            if folder_name not in DEFAULT_FOLDERS:
                print("Invalid folder name.")
                continue
            
            files = list_files(student_folder, folder_name)
            if not files:
                continue
            file_choice = input("Enter file number to open (or 'back'): ").strip()
            if file_choice.lower() == "back":
                continue
            if not file_choice.isdigit():
                print("Invalid input.")
                continue
            open_file(student_folder, folder_name, int(file_choice))
        elif choice == "search":
            query = input("Enter search query: ").strip()
            search_files(student_folder, query)
        else:
            print("Unknown command. Try again.")
```

### **1. Integrated Master Generator with Desktop**

```python
from procedural_generators import textbook_generator, assignment_generator, exam_generator
from research_notebook import add_note, load_notes
from interactive_desktop import interactive_desktop, setup_desktop
from export_helpers import export_json_to_txt
import os

DEFAULT_FOLDERS = ["Chapters", "Assignments", "Exams", "Research"]

def generate_student_resources_desktop(student_id, subject):
    print(f"Generating all resources for Student {student_id} - Subject: {subject}")
    
    # Setup desktop folders
    student_folder = setup_desktop(student_id)
    
    # --- 1. Generate Chapters ---
    for chapter_number in range(1, 4):
        chapter_file = textbook_generator.generate_chapter(student_id, subject, chapter_number)
        chapter_title = f"{subject} Chapter {chapter_number}"
        add_note(student_id, title=f"Notes: {chapter_title}",
                 content=f"Research notes for {chapter_title}",
                 tags=[subject, "Chapter", f"Chapter {chapter_number}"])
        # Export to desktop folder
        export_json_to_txt(student_id, chapter_file, f"{chapter_title}.txt")
        # Move to correct desktop folder
        os.rename(f"student_desktops/student_{student_id}/{chapter_title}.txt",
                  os.path.join(student_folder, "Chapters", f"{chapter_title}.txt"))
    
    # --- 2. Generate Assignments ---
    for assignment_number in range(1, 3):
        assignment_file = assignment_generator.generate_assignment(student_id, subject, assignment_number, difficulty='medium')
        add_note(student_id, title=f"Strategy: Assignment {assignment_number}",
                 content=f"Problem-solving strategies for Assignment {assignment_number}",
                 tags=[subject, "Assignment", f"Assignment {assignment_number}"])
        export_json_to_txt(student_id, assignment_file, f"Assignment_{assignment_number}.txt")
        os.rename(f"student_desktops/student_{student_id}/Assignment_{assignment_number}.txt",
                  os.path.join(student_folder, "Assignments", f"Assignment_{assignment_number}.txt"))
    
    # --- 3. Generate Exam ---
    exam_file = exam_generator.generate_exam(student_id, subject, exam_number=1, time_limit=60)
    add_note(student_id, title=f"Strategy: Exam 1", content="Preparation notes and key concepts for Exam 1", tags=[subject, "Exam"])
    export_json_to_txt(student_id, exam_file, "Exam_1.txt")
    os.rename(f"student_desktops/student_{student_id}/Exam_1.txt",
              os.path.join(student_folder, "Exams", "Exam_1.txt"))
    
    # --- 4. Export Research Notes ---
    research_notes_file = os.path.join(student_folder, "Research", "Research_Notes.txt")
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    with open(research_notes_file, "w") as f:
        for note in notes:
            f.write(f"TITLE: {note['title']}\nTAGS: {', '.join(note['tags'])}\nCONTENT: {note['content']}\nCREATED: {note['created_at']}\nUPDATED: {note['updated_at']}\n\n")
    print(f"Research notes exported to desktop: {research_notes_file}")
    
    print(f"All resources generated and organized on the desktop for Student {student_id}!\n")
    
    # --- 5. Launch interactive desktop ---
    interactive_desktop(student_id)
```

### **1. Full Batch Generator - `full_class_generator.py`**

```python
import json
import os
from integrated_desktop_generator import generate_student_resources_desktop

STUDENTS_DATA_FILE = "students.json"

def load_students():
    """Load student progress data or initialize empty list."""
    if os.path.exists(STUDENTS_DATA_FILE):
        with open(STUDENTS_DATA_FILE, "r") as f:
            return json.load(f)
    return []

def save_students(students_data):
    with open(STUDENTS_DATA_FILE, "w") as f:
        json.dump(students_data, f, indent=4)
    print(f"Saved progress for {len(students_data)} students.")

def generate_class_resources(student_list, subjects, launch_desktop=False):
    """
    Generate full resources for multiple students and subjects.

    student_list: list of student IDs
    subjects: list of subjects (e.g., ["Math", "Science"])
    launch_desktop: True to open interactive desktop after generation
    """
    students_data = load_students()
    
    class_summary = {}

    for student_id in student_list:
        print(f"\n=== Generating resources for Student {student_id} ===")
        student_summary = {}

        for subject in subjects:
            print(f"--- Subject: {subject} ---")
            if launch_desktop:
                # Launch interactive desktop after generation
                generate_student_resources_desktop(student_id, subject)
            else:
                # Generate resources without launching desktop
                from integrated_desktop_generator import generate_student_resources
                generate_student_resources(student_id, subject)

            # Track progress
            student_summary[subject] = {
                "chapters": 3,
                "assignments": 2,
                "exams": 1
            }
        
        class_summary[student_id] = student_summary

        # Update students.json
        students_data = [s for s in students_data if s['id'] != student_id]  # remove old record
        students_data.append({
            "id": student_id,
            "subjects": student_summary
        })

    save_students(students_data)
    
    # Print summary
    print("\n=== Class Generation Summary ===")
    for sid, subjects in class_summary.items():
        print(f"Student {sid}:")
        for subject, counts in subjects.items():
            print(f"  {subject} -> Chapters: {counts['chapters']}, Assignments: {counts['assignments']}, Exams: {counts['exams']}")
    print("\nAll resources generated successfully for the class!")
```

```python
    # OR: Generate for one student with desktop interactive launch
    # generate_class_resources([101], ["Math"], launch_desktop=True)
```

4. Updates **students.json** with progress (per subject, per student).

6. Prints a **class summary** with total resources generated.

### **1. Update `research_notebook.py` - Add Linking Support**

```python
def get_related_notes(student_id, tags):
    """
    Find all notes that match at least one tag from the given tags list.
    """
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    related = []
    for note in notes:
        if any(tag in note['tags'] for tag in tags):
            related.append(note)
    return related
```

### **2. Update Export to Desktop - Include Related Notes**

Modify the `export_json_to_txt` or the desktop export step in `integrated_desktop_generator.py` to include a **Related Notes section** at the top of the file:

```python
from research_notebook import get_related_notes

def export_resource_with_notes(student_id, json_file, txt_filename, tags, desktop_subfolder):
    """
    Export JSON resource to desktop with related notes included at the top.
    """
    student_folder = os.path.join("student_desktops", f"student_{student_id}", desktop_subfolder)

    # Load resource content
    with open(json_file, "r") as f:
        data = json.load(f)

    # Gather content for export (flatten JSON as before)
    content_lines = [f"{k.upper()}: {v}" for k, v in data.items() if not isinstance(v, list) and not isinstance(v, dict)]

    # --- Related Notes ---
    related_notes = get_related_notes(student_id, tags)
    related_lines = ["--- RELATED NOTES ---"]
    for note in related_notes:
        related_lines.append(f"TITLE: {note['title']}\nTAGS: {', '.join(note['tags'])}\nCONTENT: {note['content']}\n")
    related_lines.append("--- END RELATED NOTES ---\n")

    # Combine related notes + resource content
    full_content = related_lines + content_lines

    # Write to desktop
    os.makedirs(student_folder, exist_ok=True)
    txt_path = os.path.join(student_folder, txt_filename)
    with open(txt_path, "w") as f:
        f.write("\n".join(full_content))
    
    print(f"Exported {txt_path} with related notes")
    return txt_path
```

### **1. Enhanced Desktop Simulator with Related Notes - `interactive_desktop_linked.py`**

```python
import os
from research_notebook import load_notes, get_related_notes

DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"
DEFAULT_FOLDERS = ["Chapters", "Assignments", "Exams", "Research"]

def setup_desktop(student_id):
    """Ensure desktop folders exist."""
    student_folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
    os.makedirs(student_folder, exist_ok=True)
    for folder in DEFAULT_FOLDERS:
        os.makedirs(os.path.join(student_folder, folder), exist_ok=True)
    return student_folder

def list_files(student_folder, folder_name=None):
    folder = student_folder if not folder_name else os.path.join(student_folder, folder_name)
    files = [f for f in os.listdir(folder) if f.endswith(".txt")]
    if not files:
        print("No files found here.")
        return []
    for i, file in enumerate(files):
        print(f"{i + 1}. {file}")
    return files

def open_file_with_links(student_id, folder_name, file_index):
    student_folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
    folder = student_folder if not folder_name else os.path.join(student_folder, folder_name)
    files = [f for f in os.listdir(folder) if f.endswith(".txt")]
    
    if file_index < 1 or file_index > len(files):
        print("Invalid file number.")
        return
    
    file_to_open = os.path.join(folder, files[file_index - 1])
    
    # Load file content
    with open(file_to_open, "r") as f:
        content = f.read()
    
    # Display file with related notes prompt
    print(f"\n--- Opening {files[file_index - 1]} ---\n")
    print(content)
    
    # Find related notes from research folder
    related_notes = get_related_notes(student_id, [folder_name[:-1]])  # use folder name as tag
    
    if related_notes:
        print("\n--- RELATED NOTES ---")
        for i, note in enumerate(related_notes):
            print(f"{i + 1}. {note['title']} (Tags: {', '.join(note['tags'])})")
        print("Type number to open related note or 'back' to return.")
        
        while True:
            choice = input("Open related note: ").strip()
            if choice.lower() == "back":
                break
            if choice.isdigit() and 1 <= int(choice) <= len(related_notes):
                note = related_notes[int(choice) - 1]
                print(f"\n--- {note['title']} ---\n{note['content']}\n--- End of Note ---\n")
            else:
                print("Invalid choice. Type number or 'back'.")
    print("\n--- End of File ---\n")

def interactive_desktop_linked(student_id):
    student_folder = setup_desktop(student_id)
    
    while True:
        print("\n=== Student Desktop ===")
        print("Folders: ", ", ".join(DEFAULT_FOLDERS))
        print("Options: [open folder] [search] [exit]")
        choice = input("Enter command: ").strip().lower()
        
        if choice == "exit":
            print("Exiting desktop.")
            break
        elif choice.startswith("open"):
            parts = choice.split()
            if len(parts) < 2:
                print("Specify folder to open: Chapters, Assignments, Exams, Research")
                continue
            folder_name = parts[1].capitalize()
            if folder_name not in DEFAULT_FOLDERS:
                print("Invalid folder name.")
                continue
            
            files = list_files(student_folder, folder_name)
            if not files:
                continue
            file_choice = input("Enter file number to open (or 'back'): ").strip()
            if file_choice.lower() == "back":
                continue
            if not file_choice.isdigit():
                print("Invalid input.")
                continue
            open_file_with_links(student_id, folder_name, int(file_choice))
        elif choice == "search":
            query = input("Enter search query: ").strip()
            matches = []
            for root, _, files in os.walk(student_folder):
                for file in files:
                    if file.endswith(".txt"):
                        path = os.path.join(root, file)
                        with open(path, "r") as f:
                            if query.lower() in f.read().lower():
                                matches.append(os.path.relpath(path, student_folder))
            if matches:
                print(f"Found {len(matches)} matching files:")
                for i, match in enumerate(matches):
                    print(f"{i + 1}. {match}")
            else:
                print("No matches found.")
        else:
            print("Unknown command. Try again.")
```

```python
# Launch the linked interactive desktop
interactive_desktop_linked(STUDENT_ID)
```

### **1. Update `research_notebook.py` - Multi-Tag Related Notes & Tracking**

```python
import json
import os
from datetime import datetime

NOTES_FILE = "notes.json"
USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE = "usage_student_{student_id}.json"

def load_notes(student_id):
    """Load all notes for a student."""
    if os.path.exists(NOTES_FILE):
        with open(NOTES_FILE, "r") as f:
            return json.load(f).get(str(student_id), [])
    return []

def save_notes(student_id, notes):
    """Save notes for a student."""
    all_notes = {}
    if os.path.exists(NOTES_FILE):
        with open(NOTES_FILE, "r") as f:
            all_notes = json.load(f)
    all_notes[str(student_id)] = notes
    with open(NOTES_FILE, "w") as f:
        json.dump(all_notes, f, indent=4)

def add_note(student_id, title, content, tags):
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    note = {
        "id": len(notes) + 1,
        "title": title,
        "content": content,
        "tags": tags,
        "created_at": str(datetime.now()),
        "updated_at": str(datetime.now())
    }
    notes.append(note)
    save_notes(student_id, notes)

def get_related_notes(student_id, resource_tags):
    """Return notes that match at least one tag in resource_tags, including usage tracking."""
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    related = []
    
    # Load usage tracking
    usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
    if os.path.exists(usage_file):
        with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
            usage = json.load(f)
    else:
        usage = {}

    for note in notes:
        if any(tag in note['tags'] for tag in resource_tags):
            note_copy = note.copy()
            note_copy['read'] = usage.get(str(note['id']), False)  # track if already opened
            related.append(note_copy)
    return related

def mark_note_read(student_id, note_id):
    """Mark a note as read for a student."""
    usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
    if os.path.exists(usage_file):
        with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
            usage = json.load(f)
    else:
        usage = {}
    usage[str(note_id)] = True
    with open(usage_file, "w") as f:
        json.dump(usage, f, indent=4)
```

### **2. Update Desktop - Show Multi-Tag Related Notes with Tracking**

Modify the `open_file_with_links` function to:

- Accept a list of **tags for the resource**  
- Display **read/unread status** for each related note  
- Mark notes as **read when opened**  

```python
def open_file_with_links(student_id, folder_name, file_index, resource_tags):
    student_folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
    folder = student_folder if not folder_name else os.path.join(student_folder, folder_name)
    files = [f for f in os.listdir(folder) if f.endswith(".txt")]
    
    if file_index < 1 or file_index > len(files):
        print("Invalid file number.")
        return
    
    file_to_open = os.path.join(folder, files[file_index - 1])
    
    with open(file_to_open, "r") as f:
        content = f.read()
    
    print(f"\n--- Opening {files[file_index - 1]} ---\n")
    print(content)
    
    related_notes = get_related_notes(student_id, resource_tags)
    if related_notes:
        print("\n--- RELATED NOTES ---")
        for i, note in enumerate(related_notes):
            status = "READ" if note['read'] else "NEW"
            print(f"{i + 1}. {note['title']} (Tags: {', '.join(note['tags'])}) [{status}]")
        print("Type number to open related note, or 'back' to return.")

        while True:
            choice = input("Open related note: ").strip()
            if choice.lower() == "back":
                break
            if choice.isdigit() and 1 <= int(choice) <= len(related_notes):
                note = related_notes[int(choice) - 1]
                print(f"\n--- {note['title']} ---\n{note['content']}\n--- End of Note ---\n")
                # Mark as read
                from research_notebook import mark_note_read
                mark_note_read(student_id, note['id'])
                note['read'] = True
            else:
                print("Invalid choice. Type number or 'back'.")
    print("\n--- End of File ---\n")
```

ChatGPT
Perfect - let's implement **priority-ranked related notes** so students see the **most relevant notes first** when opening a resource.  

We'll rank notes based on:  

1. **Number of matching tags** - more matching tags = higher relevance.  
2. **Recency of creation or update** - newer notes get slight priority.  
3. **Unread status** - new notes appear before already-read notes.  

This will give a **smart, prioritized study experience**.  

---

### **1. Update `research_notebook.py` - Priority Ranking**

Add a function to rank related notes:

```python
from datetime import datetime

def get_priority_related_notes(student_id, resource_tags):
    """
    Return related notes sorted by priority:
    - Unread first
    - More tag matches first
    - Newer notes first
    """
    notes = get_related_notes(student_id, resource_tags)
    
    def note_score(note):
        # Count how many tags match
        tag_matches = sum(1 for tag in note['tags'] if tag in resource_tags)
        # Recency score: timestamp in seconds
        recency = datetime.strptime(note['updated_at'], "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f").timestamp()
        # Unread bonus
        unread_bonus = 1 if not note['read'] else 0
        # Combine score (weights can be adjusted)
        return (unread_bonus, tag_matches, recency)
    
    # Sort descending by score
    notes_sorted = sorted(notes, key=note_score, reverse=True)
    return notes_sorted
```

### **1. Add Study Recommendation Module - `study_recommendations.py`**

```python
import os
from research_notebook import load_notes, get_related_notes, mark_note_read

DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"
DEFAULT_FOLDERS = ["Chapters", "Assignments", "Exams", "Research"]

def recommend_next_resources(student_id, subjects):
    """
    Recommend which chapters, assignments, or exams the student should focus on next.
    """
    recommendations = []

    student_folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")

    for subject in subjects:
        # Check chapters
        chapter_folder = os.path.join(student_folder, "Chapters")
        if os.path.exists(chapter_folder):
            for file in os.listdir(chapter_folder):
                if subject.lower() in file.lower() and file.endswith(".txt"):
                    # Count related unread notes
                    tags = [subject] + [file.split()[1]]  # e.g., ['Math', 'Chapter1']
                    notes = get_related_notes(student_id, tags)
                    unread_count = sum(1 for n in notes if not n['read'])
                    if unread_count > 0:
                        recommendations.append({
                            "resource": file,
                            "type": "Chapter",
                            "subject": subject,
                            "unread_notes": unread_count
                        })

        # Check assignments
        assignment_folder = os.path.join(student_folder, "Assignments")
        if os.path.exists(assignment_folder):
            for file in os.listdir(assignment_folder):
                if subject.lower() in file.lower() and file.endswith(".txt"):
                    tags = [subject, "Assignment"]
                    notes = get_related_notes(student_id, tags)
                    unread_count = sum(1 for n in notes if not n['read'])
                    recommendations.append({
                        "resource": file,
                        "type": "Assignment",
                        "subject": subject,
                        "unread_notes": unread_count
                    })

        # Check exams
        exam_folder = os.path.join(student_folder, "Exams")
        if os.path.exists(exam_folder):
            for file in os.listdir(exam_folder):
                if subject.lower() in file.lower() and file.endswith(".txt"):
                    tags = [subject, "Exam"]
                    notes = get_related_notes(student_id, tags)
                    unread_count = sum(1 for n in notes if not n['read'])
                    recommendations.append({
                        "resource": file,
                        "type": "Exam",
                        "subject": subject,
                        "unread_notes": unread_count
                    })

    # Sort recommendations: unread notes first, then type priority (Chapter > Assignment > Exam)
    type_priority = {"Chapter": 3, "Assignment": 2, "Exam": 1}
    recommendations_sorted = sorted(
        recommendations,
        key=lambda r: (r['unread_notes'], type_priority[r['type']]),
        reverse=True
    )
    
    return recommendations_sorted
```

---

### **1. Teacher Progress Reporting Module - `teacher_reports.py`**

```python
import os
import csv
from research_notebook import load_notes
from interactive_desktop_linked import DESKTOP_FOLDER, DEFAULT_FOLDERS
from research_notebook import USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE
import json

def generate_teacher_report(student_list, subjects, output_file="teacher_progress.csv"):
    """
    Generate a progress report for teachers summarizing notes read, assignments, and exams.
    """
    report_data = []

    for student_id in student_list:
        student_folder = os.path.join(DESKTOP_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}")
        
        # Load notes and usage
        usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
        if os.path.exists(usage_file):
            with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
                usage = json.load(f)
        else:
            usage = {}

        notes = load_notes(student_id)
        total_notes = len(notes)
        read_notes = sum(1 for n in notes if usage.get(str(n['id']), False))
        unread_notes = total_notes - read_notes

        for subject in subjects:
            # Count assignments and exams
            assignment_folder = os.path.join(student_folder, "Assignments")
            exam_folder = os.path.join(student_folder, "Exams")

            assignments = [f for f in os.listdir(assignment_folder) if subject.lower() in f.lower()] if os.path.exists(assignment_folder) else []
            exams = [f for f in os.listdir(exam_folder) if subject.lower() in f.lower()] if os.path.exists(exam_folder) else []

            report_data.append({
                "Student ID": student_id,
                "Subject": subject,
                "Total Notes": total_notes,
                "Read Notes": read_notes,
                "Unread Notes": unread_notes,
                "Assignments": len(assignments),
                "Exams": len(exams)
            })

    # Export report to CSV
    with open(output_file, "w", newline="") as csvfile:
        fieldnames = ["Student ID", "Subject", "Total Notes", "Read Notes", "Unread Notes", "Assignments", "Exams"]
        writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
        writer.writeheader()
        for row in report_data:
            writer.writerow(row)

    print(f"Teacher progress report generated: {output_file}")
```

---

### **2. Example Usage**

```python
if __name__ == "__main__":
    STUDENT_LIST = [101, 102, 103, 104, 105]
    SUBJECTS = ["Math", "Science", "History"]

    generate_teacher_report(STUDENT_LIST, SUBJECTS)
```

---

### **3. What the Report Includes**

| Student ID | Subject | Total Notes | Read Notes | Unread Notes | Assignments | Exams |
|------------|--------|------------|------------|--------------|------------|------|
| 101        | Math   | 20         | 12         | 8            | 2          | 1    |
| 101        | Science| 18         | 10         | 8            | 2          | 1    |

- `Total Notes`: Total research notes for the student.  
- `Read Notes`: Notes the student has already opened.  
- `Unread Notes`: Notes not yet opened.  
- `Assignments` & `Exams`: Counts per subject.

- Add **graphical dashboard** integration for visual analysis.

Do you want me to implement **automated grading** next?

ChatGPT
Perfect - let's implement **automated grading** for assignments and exams, completing the full loop from **resource generation → interactive study → submission → grading → teacher report**.  

The system will:  

1. **Accept student submissions** (text-based or structured answer files).  
2. **Compare against answer keys** generated with the assignments/exams.  
3. **Score automatically** and store results.  
4. **Update teacher progress reports** with grades and completion status.  

---

### **1. Grading Module - `auto_grader.py`**

```python
import os
import json
from datetime import datetime

# Folder structure
STUDENT_DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"
GRADES_FILE_TEMPLATE = "grades_student_{student_id}.json"

def grade_student_submission(student_id, subject, assignment_name, answer_key_file, submission_file):
    """
    Compare a student's submission with the answer key and compute a grade.
    """
    # Load answer key
    with open(answer_key_file, "r") as f:
        answer_key = json.load(f)

    # Load student submission
    with open(submission_file, "r") as f:
        submission = json.load(f)

    # Simple scoring: match answers by key
    total_questions = len(answer_key)
    correct = 0
    for question, answer in answer_key.items():
        student_answer = submission.get(question, "")
        if str(student_answer).strip().lower() == str(answer).strip().lower():
            correct += 1

    score = round((correct / total_questions) * 100, 2)

    # Save or update grades
    grades_file = GRADES_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
    if os.path.exists(grades_file):
        with open(grades_file, "r") as f:
            grades_data = json.load(f)
    else:
        grades_data = {}

    grades_data.setdefault(subject, {})
    grades_data[subject][assignment_name] = {
        "score": score,
        "graded_at": str(datetime.now())
    }

    with open(grades_file, "w") as f:
        json.dump(grades_data, f, indent=4)

    print(f"Student {student_id} scored {score}% on {assignment_name}")
    return score
```

```python
if __name__ == "__main__":
    STUDENT_ID = 101
    SUBJECT = "Math"
    ASSIGNMENT_NAME = "Assignment_1"
    
    ANSWER_KEY_FILE = "answer_keys/Math_Assignment_1.json"
    STUDENT_SUBMISSION_FILE = "submissions/student_101/Math_Assignment_1.json"
    
    grade_student_submission(STUDENT_ID, SUBJECT, ASSIGNMENT_NAME, ANSWER_KEY_FILE, STUDENT_SUBMISSION_FILE)
```

5. Can be integrated with **teacher reports** to show performance alongside notes read and resource completion.

ChatGPT
Perfect - let's implement **batch grading** so teachers can **automatically grade an entire class's assignments and exams in one command** and update progress reports simultaneously.  

This will:  

1. **Iterate through all students and subjects**.  
2. **Check for submitted assignments/exams** in their folders.  
3. **Compare with answer keys**.  
4. **Store grades per student**.  
5. **Optionally update teacher progress reports** immediately.

### **1. Batch Grading Module - `batch_grader.py`**

```python
import os
import json
from auto_grader import grade_student_submission

# Folder structure for submissions and answer keys
SUBMISSIONS_FOLDER = "submissions"
ANSWER_KEYS_FOLDER = "answer_keys"

def batch_grade_class(student_list, subjects):
    """
    Batch grade all students for all subjects, updating their grades files.
    """
    print("=== Starting Batch Grading ===")
    
    for student_id in student_list:
        print(f"\nGrading Student {student_id}...")
        for subject in subjects:
            # Assignment grading
            assignment_folder = os.path.join(SUBMISSIONS_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}", "Assignments")
            answer_assignment_folder = os.path.join(ANSWER_KEYS_FOLDER, subject, "Assignments")
            if os.path.exists(assignment_folder):
                for file in os.listdir(assignment_folder):
                    if file.endswith(".json"):
                        submission_file = os.path.join(assignment_folder, file)
                        answer_file = os.path.join(answer_assignment_folder, file)
                        if os.path.exists(answer_file):
                            grade_student_submission(student_id, subject, file, answer_file, submission_file)

            # Exam grading
            exam_folder = os.path.join(SUBMISSIONS_FOLDER, f"student_{student_id}", "Exams")
            answer_exam_folder = os.path.join(ANSWER_KEYS_FOLDER, subject, "Exams")
            if os.path.exists(exam_folder):
                for file in os.listdir(exam_folder):
                    if file.endswith(".json"):
                        submission_file = os.path.join(exam_folder, file)
                        answer_file = os.path.join(answer_exam_folder, file)
                        if os.path.exists(answer_file):
                            grade_student_submission(student_id, subject, file, answer_file, submission_file)
    print("\n=== Batch Grading Completed ===")
```

---

### **2. Example Usage**

```python
if __name__ == "__main__":
    STUDENT_LIST = [101, 102, 103, 104, 105]
    SUBJECTS = ["Math", "Science", "History"]

    batch_grade_class(STUDENT_LIST, SUBJECTS)
```

4. Stores grades in `grades_student_{student_id}.json`.

ChatGPT
Absolutely - we can extend the system to include a **Board of Education (BoE) workflow** for teachers, administrators, and quality assurance. This will layer an additional **governance, review, and archival system** on top of the student resources, progress tracking, and grading.  

Here's how it could work:

---

## **1. Board of Education Workflow Overview**

### **Actors**
1. **Teachers**
   - Submit grades, assignment/exam designs, and student progress reports.
   - Flag anomalies or exceptions for review.

2. **Board of Education (QA & Review Panel)**
   - Reviews teacher submissions for **accuracy, completeness, and adherence to protocols**.
   - Resolves issues such as misgraded exams, missing notes, or misaligned resources.
   - Approves final scores and progress tracking.

3. **Archival System**
   - Maintains a **historical record** of each student's progress, grades, and QA outcomes.
   - Allows **longitudinal tracking** across multiple years/subjects.
   - Supports audit requests or system-wide reporting.

---

### **2. Functional Components**

#### **A. Review Queue**
- Teachers submit **resource grading and progress reports** to the BoE.
- The BoE dashboard shows **pending reviews** with priority based on flagged issues or discrepancies.

#### **B. QA Review Process**
- BoE can **approve**, **reject**, or **modify submissions**.
- Issues are logged, with notes for **protocol adjustments**.
- Can trigger **student notifications** for corrections if needed.

#### **C. Archival System**
- Stores **approved student progress snapshots**.
- Each snapshot includes:
  - Grades
  - Notes read/unread
  - Assignment/exam completion
  - QA review metadata (reviewer, timestamp, resolution)
- Supports **queries** like:
  - Student history over multiple years
  - Audit of teacher grading behavior
  - Policy compliance tracking

---

### **3. Proposed Folder/Data Structure**

```
board_of_education/
├─ review_queue/
│  ├─ student_{id}_subject_report.json
├─ approved/
│  ├─ student_{id}_subject_report.json
├─ archived/
│  ├─ student_{id}/
│     ├─ year_2026/
│     │   ├─ subject_progress.json
│     │   ├─ QA_log.json
├─ logs/
│  ├─ BoE_activity_log.json
```

- **review_queue/** - Submissions awaiting QA review.
- **approved/** - QA-approved reports ready to be merged into archival history.
- **archived/** - Long-term storage of approved student progress.
- **logs/** - Tracks all BoE actions and resolutions.

---

### **4. Example BoE QA Module - `board_of_education.py`**

```python
import os
import json
from datetime import datetime

REVIEW_QUEUE = "board_of_education/review_queue"
APPROVED = "board_of_education/approved"
ARCHIVE = "board_of_education/archived"
LOGS = "board_of_education/logs"

def submit_for_review(student_id, subject, report_file):
    """
    Teacher submits a report to the Board of Education review queue.
    """
    os.makedirs(REVIEW_QUEUE, exist_ok=True)
    review_file = f"{student_id}_{subject}_report.json"
    dest = os.path.join(REVIEW_QUEUE, review_file)
    with open(report_file, "r") as src, open(dest, "w") as dst:
        dst.write(src.read())
    print(f"Report submitted for review: {dest}")

def review_report(student_id, subject, action, reviewer, notes=""):
    """
    BoE reviews a report: action = 'approve', 'reject', 'modify'
    """
    review_file = os.path.join(REVIEW_QUEUE, f"{student_id}_{subject}_report.json")
    if not os.path.exists(review_file):
        print("No report found for review.")
        return
    
    # Load report
    with open(review_file, "r") as f:
        report_data = json.load(f)
    
    # Update review metadata
    report_data.setdefault("QA_review", {})
    report_data["QA_review"].update({
        "reviewer": reviewer,
        "action": action,
        "notes": notes,
        "timestamp": str(datetime.now())
    })
    
    # Move to approved or reject
    if action == "approve":
        os.makedirs(APPROVED, exist_ok=True)
        with open(os.path.join(APPROVED, f"{student_id}_{subject}_report.json"), "w") as f:
            json.dump(report_data, f, indent=4)
        # Archive student progress
        archive_student_progress(student_id, subject, report_data)
        print(f"Report approved and archived for student {student_id}, subject {subject}")
    elif action == "reject":
        print(f"Report rejected: {notes}")
    elif action == "modify":
        with open(review_file, "w") as f:
            json.dump(report_data, f, indent=4)
        print(f"Report updated for modification: {notes}")
    
    # Log QA action
    log_QA_action(student_id, subject, reviewer, action, notes)

def archive_student_progress(student_id, subject, report_data, year=2026):
    """
    Save approved student progress into the archival system.
    """
    archive_folder = os.path.join(ARCHIVE, f"student_{student_id}", f"year_{year}")
    os.makedirs(archive_folder, exist_ok=True)
    
    # Save progress
    progress_file = os.path.join(archive_folder, f"{subject}_progress.json")
    with open(progress_file, "w") as f:
        json.dump(report_data, f, indent=4)
    
    # Optional: maintain a QA log per student/year
    qa_log_file = os.path.join(archive_folder, "QA_log.json")
    if os.path.exists(qa_log_file):
        with open(qa_log_file, "r") as f:
            qa_logs = json.load(f)
    else:
        qa_logs = []
    qa_logs.append({
        "subject": subject,
        "review_timestamp": str(datetime.now()),
        "report_snapshot": report_data
    })
    with open(qa_log_file, "w") as f:
        json.dump(qa_logs, f, indent=4)

def log_QA_action(student_id, subject, reviewer, action, notes):
    """
    Log all Board of Education actions for audit.
    """
    os.makedirs(LOGS, exist_ok=True)
    log_file = os.path.join(LOGS, "BoE_activity_log.json")
    if os.path.exists(log_file):
        with open(log_file, "r") as f:
            logs = json.load(f)
    else:
        logs = []
    
    logs.append({
        "student_id": student_id,
        "subject": subject,
        "reviewer": reviewer,
        "action": action,
        "notes": notes,
        "timestamp": str(datetime.now())
    })
    with open(log_file, "w") as f:
        json.dump(logs, f, indent=4)
```

### **5. How This Works in Practice**

1. **Teacher submits** student progress/grading report to the **BoE review queue**.  
2. **BoE reviewers** (could be multiple members) **approve, reject, or modify** reports.  
3. **Approved reports** are automatically **archived** per student/year.  
4. **Rejected or modified reports** remain in the queue until resolved.  
5. All actions are **logged** for audit and protocol compliance.

  - Notify teachers or students if issues are detected or reports rejected.

### **1. Dashboard Module - `teacher_dashboard.py`**

```python
import os
import json
from board_of_education import REVIEW_QUEUE, APPROVED, archive_student_progress, log_QA_action
from research_notebook import load_notes, USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE

DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"

def teacher_dashboard(student_list, subjects, viewer="teacher"):
    """
    Interactive dashboard for teachers or Board of Education members.
    viewer = "teacher" or "BoE"
    """
    print(f"\n=== Welcome to the {'Teacher' if viewer=='teacher' else 'BoE'} Dashboard ===")
    
    while True:
        print("\nOptions:")
        print("1. View Student Progress")
        print("2. Submit Report to BoE" if viewer=="teacher" else "")
        print("3. Review Pending Reports" if viewer=="BoE" else "")
        print("4. Exit Dashboard")
        
        choice = input("Select option: ").strip()
        
        if choice == "1":
            view_student_progress(student_list, subjects)
        
        elif choice == "2" and viewer=="teacher":
            submit_report_interactive(student_list, subjects)
        
        elif choice == "3" and viewer=="BoE":
            review_pending_reports()
        
        elif choice == "4":
            break
        else:
            print("Invalid choice. Try again.")

```

### **2. View Student Progress**

```python
def view_student_progress(student_list, subjects):
    print("\n--- Student Progress ---")
    for student_id in student_list:
        usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
        usage = {}
        if os.path.exists(usage_file):
            with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
                usage = json.load(f)
        notes = load_notes(student_id)
        total_notes = len(notes)
        read_notes = sum(1 for n in notes if usage.get(str(n['id']), False))
        print(f"\nStudent {student_id}: {read_notes}/{total_notes} notes read")
```

### **3. Submit Report to BoE (Teacher)**

```python
def submit_report_interactive(student_list, subjects):
    student_id = input("Enter Student ID to submit report: ").strip()
    subject = input("Enter Subject: ").strip()
    
    # Build report data
    usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
    usage = {}
    if os.path.exists(usage_file):
        with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
            usage = json.load(f)
    notes = load_notes(student_id)
    total_notes = len(notes)
    read_notes = sum(1 for n in notes if usage.get(str(n['id']), False))
    
    report_data = {
        "student_id": student_id,
        "subject": subject,
        "total_notes": total_notes,
        "read_notes": read_notes,
        "unread_notes": total_notes - read_notes
    }
    
    os.makedirs(REVIEW_QUEUE, exist_ok=True)
    report_file = os.path.join(REVIEW_QUEUE, f"{student_id}_{subject}_report.json")
    with open(report_file, "w") as f:
        json.dump(report_data, f, indent=4)
    print(f"Report submitted to BoE review queue: {report_file}")
```

### **4. Review Pending Reports (BoE)**

```python
def review_pending_reports():
    pending_files = [f for f in os.listdir(REVIEW_QUEUE) if f.endswith(".json")]
    if not pending_files:
        print("No pending reports for review.")
        return
    
    for idx, file in enumerate(pending_files, 1):
        print(f"{idx}. {file}")
    
    choice = input("Select report to review (number) or 'back': ").strip()
    if choice.lower() == "back":
        return
    if not choice.isdigit() or not (1 <= int(choice) <= len(pending_files)):
        print("Invalid selection.")
        return
    
    file_to_review = pending_files[int(choice)-1]
    file_path = os.path.join(REVIEW_QUEUE, file_to_review)
    
    with open(file_path, "r") as f:
        report_data = json.load(f)
    print(f"\n--- Report ---\n{json.dumps(report_data, indent=4)}\n")
    
    action = input("Action [approve/reject/modify]: ").strip().lower()
    reviewer = input("Reviewer name: ").strip()
    notes = input("Optional notes: ").strip()
    
    if action == "approve":
        os.makedirs(APPROVED, exist_ok=True)
        approved_path = os.path.join(APPROVED, file_to_review)
        with open(approved_path, "w") as f:
            json.dump(report_data, f, indent=4)
        archive_student_progress(report_data["student_id"], report_data["subject"], report_data)
        print(f"Report approved and archived for student {report_data['student_id']}")
    elif action == "reject":
        print(f"Report rejected: {notes}")
    elif action == "modify":
        with open(file_path, "w") as f:
            json.dump(report_data, f, indent=4)
        print(f"Report updated for modification: {notes}")
    
    log_QA_action(report_data["student_id"], report_data["subject"], reviewer, action, notes)
```

Perfect - let's implement a **visual dashboard** for teachers and the BoE, giving a **graphical overview** of student progress, notes completion, grades, pending QA reviews, and approvals/rejections.  

We'll use **Python with Matplotlib and optionally Plotly for interactivity**, producing **charts and graphs** that integrate with our existing system.  

---

### **1. Visual Dashboard Module - `visual_dashboard.py`**

```python
import os
import json
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from board_of_education import APPROVED, REVIEW_QUEUE, LOGS
from research_notebook import load_notes, USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE

DESKTOP_FOLDER = "student_desktops"

def generate_visual_dashboard(student_list, subjects):
    """
    Generate a visual overview of:
    - Notes completion
    - Grades distribution
    - Pending BoE reviews
    - QA approvals/rejections
    """
    # --- Notes Completion ---
    student_names = []
    completion_percent = []

    for student_id in student_list:
        usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
        usage = {}
        if os.path.exists(usage_file):
            with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
                usage = json.load(f)
        notes = load_notes(student_id)
        total_notes = len(notes)
        read_notes = sum(1 for n in notes if usage.get(str(n['id']), False))
        percent = (read_notes / total_notes) * 100 if total_notes else 0
        student_names.append(str(student_id))
        completion_percent.append(percent)

    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
    plt.bar(student_names, completion_percent, color='skyblue')
    plt.title("Notes Completion (%) per Student")
    plt.xlabel("Student ID")
    plt.ylabel("Completion %")
    plt.ylim(0, 100)
    plt.show()

    # --- Pending BoE Reviews ---
    pending_files = [f for f in os.listdir(REVIEW_QUEUE) if f.endswith(".json")] if os.path.exists(REVIEW_QUEUE) else []
    print(f"\nPending Reports for BoE Review: {len(pending_files)}")
    for f in pending_files:
        print(f"- {f}")

    # --- QA Approvals / Rejections ---
    log_file = os.path.join(LOGS, "BoE_activity_log.json")
    approvals, rejections, modifications = 0, 0, 0
    if os.path.exists(log_file):
        with open(log_file, "r") as f:
            logs = json.load(f)
        for entry in logs:
            if entry["action"] == "approve":
                approvals += 1
            elif entry["action"] == "reject":
                rejections += 1
            elif entry["action"] == "modify":
                modifications += 1

    plt.figure(figsize=(6, 6))
    plt.pie([approvals, rejections, modifications],
            labels=["Approved", "Rejected", "Modified"],
            autopct="%1.1f%%",
            colors=["green", "red", "orange"])
    plt.title("BoE QA Actions Overview")
    plt.show()

    # --- Grades Distribution (Approved Reports) ---
    grades = []
    for file in os.listdir(APPROVED) if os.path.exists(APPROVED) else []:
        file_path = os.path.join(APPROVED, file)
        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            data = json.load(f)
            if "grade" in data:
                grades.append(data["grade"])
            elif "score" in data:
                grades.append(data["score"])
    if grades:
        plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
        plt.hist(grades, bins=10, color='purple', edgecolor='black')
        plt.title("Grades Distribution (Approved Reports)")
        plt.xlabel("Score")
        plt.ylabel("Number of Students")
        plt.show()
    else:
        print("No grades found in approved reports yet.")
```

---

   - Shows % of notes read per student.  
   - Quickly identifies students who need support.  

2. **Pending BoE Reviews**  
   - Prints list of reports awaiting QA approval.  
   - Keeps reviewers aware of backlog.  

3. **QA Actions Pie Chart**  
   - Shows proportion of approved, rejected, and modified reports.  
   - Visualizes BoE activity trends.  

4. **Grades Distribution Histogram**  
   - Shows performance of students across subjects.  
   - Helps detect low/high performing students.

### **1. Dashboard Integration: Study Recommendations**

We'll use the **`recommend_next_resources`** function you already implemented to fetch recommendations for each student and show them visually.

```python
from study_recommendations import recommend_next_resources

def dashboard_with_recommendations(student_list, subjects):
    """
    Enhanced visual dashboard that integrates dynamic study recommendations.
    """
    print("\n=== Intelligent School Dashboard ===")
    
    # --- Notes Completion Chart ---
    student_names = []
    completion_percent = []
    for student_id in student_list:
        usage_file = USAGE_FILE_TEMPLATE.format(student_id=student_id)
        usage = {}
        if os.path.exists(usage_file):
            with open(usage_file, "r") as f:
                usage = json.load(f)
        notes = load_notes(student_id)
        total_notes = len(notes)
        read_notes = sum(1 for n in notes if usage.get(str(n['id']), False))
        percent = (read_notes / total_notes) * 100 if total_notes else 0
        student_names.append(str(student_id))
        completion_percent.append(percent)

    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
    plt.bar(student_names, completion_percent, color='skyblue')
    plt.title("Notes Completion (%) per Student")
    plt.xlabel("Student ID")
    plt.ylabel("Completion %")
    plt.ylim(0, 100)
    plt.show()

    # --- Study Recommendations Table ---
    print("\n--- Dynamic Study Recommendations ---")
    for student_id in student_list:
        print(f"\nStudent {student_id}:")
        recs = recommend_next_resources(student_id, subjects)
        if recs:
            for r in recs[:5]:  # top 5 recommendations
                print(f" - {r['resource']} ({r['type']}, {r['unread_notes']} unread notes)")
        else:
            print(" - All resources reviewed!")

    # --- Pending BoE Reviews ---
    pending_files = [f for f in os.listdir(REVIEW_QUEUE) if f.endswith(".json")] if os.path.exists(REVIEW_QUEUE) else []
    print(f"\nPending Reports for BoE Review: {len(pending_files)}")
    for f in pending_files:
        print(f"- {f}")

    # --- QA Approvals / Rejections Pie Chart ---
    log_file = os.path.join(LOGS, "BoE_activity_log.json")
    approvals, rejections, modifications = 0, 0, 0
    if os.path.exists(log_file):
        with open(log_file, "r") as f:
            logs = json.load(f)
        for entry in logs:
            if entry["action"] == "approve":
                approvals += 1
            elif entry["action"] == "reject":
                rejections += 1
            elif entry["action"] == "modify":
                modifications += 1

    plt.figure(figsize=(6, 6))
    plt.pie([approvals, rejections, modifications],
            labels=["Approved", "Rejected", "Modified"],
            autopct="%1.1f%%",
            colors=["green", "red", "orange"])
    plt.title("BoE QA Actions Overview")
    plt.show()

    # --- Grades Distribution (Approved Reports) ---
    grades = []
    for file in os.listdir(APPROVED) if os.path.exists(APPROVED) else []:
        file_path = os.path.join(APPROVED, file)
        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            data = json.load(f)
            if "grade" in data:
                grades.append(data["grade"])
            elif "score" in data:
                grades.append(data["score"])
    if grades:
        plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
        plt.hist(grades, bins=10, color='purple', edgecolor='black')
        plt.title("Grades Distribution (Approved Reports)")
        plt.xlabel("Score")
        plt.ylabel("Number of Students")
        plt.show()
    else:
        print("No grades found in approved reports yet.")
```

4. **QA Actions Pie Chart** - visualizes approvals, rejections, and modifications.  
5. **Grades Distribution Histogram** - tracks class performance.
